The energy consumption and GHG emissions for the baseline year 2019 were determined through an activity-based approach. This approach enabled the development of comprehensive data on energy consumption, allowing for a more accurate assessment of energy use. 
SECAP focuses exclusively on the actions of the İstanbul Metropolitan 
Municipality, so separate 
Building 
Energy Improvement and Energy Action and Mitigation Plans have been created for both the İstanbul City and the İstanbul 
Metropolitan 
Municipality (IMM).
Main benefits of the proposed mitigation actions in İstanbul will be:
1. 
Reduced energy consumption and carbon emissions: improving energy efficiency in building would lead to lower energy consumption and carbon emissions, helping to mitigate climate change and improve air quality in İstanbul.
2. 
Lower costs: 
Implementing energy efficiency measures can help reduce natural gas and electricity costs, as well as maintenance costs for buildings, ultimately leading to lower overall expenses for citizens in İstanbul.
3. 
Enhanced quality of life: 
By reducing energy and carbon emissions, improving air quality both indoors and outdoors, and increasing energy efficiency, the quality of life for İstanbul citizens could be significantly enhanced.
4. 
Increased regional renewable energy: As renewable energy production increases, fossil fuel consumption decreases, digitalization in electrification and energy is implemented, and micro smart grids are established, both energy supply security and more suitable energy will be achieved. This will result in a more sustainable energy system.
Overall, increased energy efficiency in the building sector in İstanbul would be a beneficial move providing significant economic, social, and environmental benefits, making it a worthwhile investment for the city and its citizens.
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 206]
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 208]
INTRODUCTION
Connecting Europe and Asia, İstanbul is a city famous for its rich history, vibrant culture and stunning architecture. As of 
2023, the population of İstanbul has reached 15.907.95158 and its urban area has reached 125.000 hectares. It hosts a diverse population with a rich demographic structure and various transportation options that serve its visitors every day. Over 12 million foreign visitors come to İstanbul each year. From the traditional modes of transport like ferries and trams to the modern options like buses and metro lines, İstanbul has a transport system that is constantly evolving to meet the needs of its people and visitors.
As of 2022, there are 26.482.847 motor land vehicles with an average age of 
14,8 in Türkiye. The high average age is disadvantageous both in respect of fuel economy and environment. However, according to the latest available data from the İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality, there were 4.940.010 registered motor vehicles in İstanbul as of the end of 2022.
Buses are the most common form of public transportation in İstanbul. There are 6.470 buses as of 2022 in İstanbul that provide transportation to millions of passengers every day. These buses are operated by İETT and cover different routes throughout the city. The average age of buses is 9,5 years as of the end of 
2022, with the newest models renewed with modern technology and amenities such as air conditioning, free Wi-Fi, and 
USB charging ports. The buses of İETT provide transportation for over 1 billion passengers annually. However, the main challenges faced by the bus system in İstanbul are traffic congestion, insufficient bus lanes, and insufficient capacity during peak hours. The main targets for the bus system in İstanbul is to shorten travel times with separated bus lanes, ensure the continuity of line optimization studies, integrate smart transportation systems, increase accessibility, safety and security for all, and increase service quality by minimizing environmental negative effects.

[Page 209]
Trams are another popular form of public transportation in İstanbul. The trams cover several routes across the city, including the historic and tourist areas. These trams are operated by İstanbul Electricity, Tramway, and Tunnel 
Company (İETT) and offer transportation for millions of passengers every year. In terms of journeys per year, the trams provide transportation for over 150 million passengers. The main challenge faced by the tram system in İstanbul is the limited capacity during peak hours. 
Trams
The metro is a rapid transit system that provides transportation to millions of passengers in İstanbul. 
There are currently eleven metro lines with 133 stations in İstanbul, with more under construction or in the planning stage. The metro lines cover different parts of the city and are operated by METRO İstanbul. 
The fleet size of the metro trains is significant, with the newest models accommodating up to 1.200 passengers. 
In terms of journeys per year, the metro provides transportation for over 757 million passengers. However, the main 
Metro challenge faced by the metro system in İstanbul is the high construction costs and long construction times for new lines. The target for the metro system in İstanbul is to expand the network to connect more areas of the city and reduce the reliance on private cars.
Nevertheless, the transportation sector plays an important role for preparation of IMM SECAP, as it is one of the main macro-sectors that should be described in SECAP, according to the Reporting guidance of the Covenant of Mayors for 
Climate and Energy (CoM). The transportation sector in İstanbul is responsible for 28% of total emissions and the single most significant source, on-road transportation. 
In order to change the situation and to prevent increasement of vehicles and 
CO2 emissions it is needed to increase energy efficiency and usage of renewables, to build a sustainable transport system in country, increase transport modes and integration between modes, reduce unit fuel consumption of vehicles, and develop policies and strategies that minimizes damage to the environment. İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality

[Page 210]
THE MAIN LEGISLATION 
Main legal acts for increasing energy efficiency and reducing CO2 emissions in transport sector are as follows:
The Energy Efficiency Strategy, a major document which addresses energy efficiency in transport in our country, aims to reduce unit fossil fuel consumption of motor vehicles, increase the share of railroads in passenger and freight transport and of urban public transport, prevent unnecessary fuel consumption in urban transport, and reduce emissions harmful to the environment.
The 
Climate 
Change 
Action 
Plan 
2011-2023 aims, among other things, to use transport modes in a balanced way for passenger and freight transport, restructure urban transport in line with sustainable transport principles, scale up the use of alternative fuels and clean car technologies, and improve energy efficiency in the sector.
In addition, there are measures for the transport sector in the National Intelligent 
Transport Systems Strategy (2014-2023) of the Ministry of Transport, Maritime 
Affairs and Communications which aims to adapt information and communication technologies to the transport sector.
The Energy Efficiency Law No. 5627 enforced in 2007 defines its fundamental purpose as to use energy effectively, avoid waste, ease the burden of energy costs on the economy, and improve efficiency in using energy resources and energy to protect the environment.
The National Climate Change Strategy of 
2010-2023 aims to increase energy efficiency and reduce greenhouse gas emissions in buildings, industry, transport and energy sectors.
The National Energy Efficiency Action 
Plan (2017-2023) sets measures to be taken regarding the transportation sector to increase energy efficiency and reduce 
CO2 emissions. Below there are the general actions of the plan regarding the transport sector:
• 
Promoting energy efficient vehicles by introducing tax advantages for highly energy efficient, low emission, environment-friendly, small motor volume vehicles including fuel-cell, electric and hybrid vehicles.
• 
Develop benchmarking on alternative fuels and new technologies which will scale up vehicles that use alternative fuels and/or new technologies.
• 
Develop and improve bicycle and pedestrian transport to scale up 
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 211]
zero-emission transport to ensure sustainable urban and regional transport.
• 
Reduce traffic density in cities: 
Discourage use of automobiles. 
Implement effective control of street-parking of vehicles, dissuasive parking fee system, and establish smart parking area systems in order to reduce traffic density in urban centers. 
• 
Promote public transport. Develop infrastructure and mobility plans to promote public transport systems.
• 
Develop and implement institutional restructuring for urban transport: 
Support the institutional restructuring of local organizations which will prepare national and local transport master plans to ensure sustainable transport.
• 
Strengthen maritime transport. 
Improve current technology, infrastructure and relevant legislative framework including energy efficiency to strengthen maritime transport.
• 
Strengthen rail transport. Transfer a part of cargo and passenger transport from road to railways on account of high-capacity rail infrastructure.
The Transportation and Logistics Master 
Plan 2023-2053
Main objects of the plan are to reduce logistics costs and increase service/response speed in line with sustainable mobility, to carry out efficient logistics activities on a regional basis.
• 
In cooperation with non-governmental organizations representing the sector, maintenance, and repair services of transportation and logistics infrastructure, vehicles and equipment will be developed to spread the freight traffic over time by using the flexibility in loading and delivery times and to realize optimizations that will benefit from the logistics infrastructure at the highest level.
• 
Efficiency and productivity will be increased in transportation.
• 
Efficiency, productivity, and service quality will be increased in logistics centers.
• 
Cooperation will be made with relevant institutions in order to increase efficiency and productivity in customs.
• 
The quality and competency of transportation and logistics services will be increased, and costs will be reduced.
İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality

[Page 212]
İstanbul has a well-developed complex transport system, with the provision of multiple modes of public transport, with extensive walking and cycling and private car use. As the most economically prosperous region within Türkiye it also has extensive transport networks and connections to the rest of the country.
Reducing emissions from energy consumption in buildings and transportation largely coincides with the strategy and activities of IMM till 2050. In addition, due to the city's high population, traffic density and energy costs, citizens' knowledge, and willingness to reduce emissions such as public transportation, clean energy and energy efficiency will support the work of IMM in these areas.
5.3. 
TRANSPORT SECTOR IN IMM 
In İstanbul, where more than 30 million journeys are made daily, the public transportation system plays a vital role in supporting the economy and providing citizens with access to basic services such as jobs, health, and education with healthy and environmentally sustainable options. 
In recent years, heavy investment has been made in the city's public transport system. 
74% of public transport journeys are made by rubber-tyre types (bus and minibus). If the expansion of İstanbul's rail system network is completed as planned, the share of the rail system in public transport will nearly double from 24% to 47%. The rail system network is growing gradually, and the public transportation system is developing in parallel with the widespread use of smart transportation technologies. İstanbul has a total rail system network of 
262,15 km and a rail system project with a total length of 208,90 km is under construction (Figure 21). 103,30 km of these projects are carried out by the Ministry of 
Transport and Infrastructure. Metrobus, 
Marmaray and other rail system lines have been put into service in the city in recent years. 
Public transport projects have increased social inclusion and improved access to economic, social, and cultural opportunities for people living in the periphery of the city. 
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 213]
İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality
Another issue that needs to be addressed in terms of the public transportation system in İstanbul is sea transportation. The city has four different coasts, in the north and south, in addition to the Bosphorus and Golden Horn coasts. With a coastline longer than 500 km, İstanbul has a great potential in terms of sea transportation.
The share of sea transportation in daily public transportation journeys in İstanbul is approximately 2,5%. Seaside crossings are at the forefront of the journeys where sea transportation can be used more effectively in İstanbul. 
Active modes of transportation (walking and cycling) play a very important role in reducing the environmental impacts of transportation and contributing to a healthy life. It is very important to plan and design streets in a way that supports and encourages walking and cycling, thereby improving the quality of life of the citizens. 
However, walking on city streets is not safe and enjoyable due to low infrastructure standards, street crowds (trash cans, street lamps, signs, temporary barriers, etc.), occupation of sidewalks by automobiles and shopkeepers (shops, cafes). On the other hand, the awareness of the citizens about the benefits of walking is also low. Although the proportion of trips made on foot is high (around 40% of total trips), İstanbul cannot be described as a walkable city in terms of the opportunities it offers to pedestrians. 
Figure 21. İstanbul Railway Network Map

[Page 214]
In İstanbul, the bicycle is used for sports and recreation activities rather than being a means of transportation. Despite some recent institutional developments, planning and infrastructure works, there is a need for significant breakthroughs in issues such as a holistic and safe bicycle network and bicycle parking. As of the end of 2022, there are 451,85 km of bicycle paths in İstanbul. In addition, a bicycle sharing program is implemented throughout the city. Cycling plays an important role in the first and last kilometer journeys in İstanbul. To this end, feeder bike routes need to be created to connect public transport stops and hubs with important services such as housing, work, and education.
Micro-mobility options such as electric bikes and electric scooters are becoming increasingly popular these days. Although they are not seen as active mobility, micro-mobility options are technologies that cannot be ignored. It is very important to implement electric sharing services as this service is getting more popular also in other big cities.
In 2019, the transportation sector in İstanbul covers 28% of the total GHG emissions. 
Road transport is the most important source of GHG emissions in the transport sector. This activity comes mostly from private cars and a significant number of buses. 
The 2019 inventory presented in Baseline Emission Inventory Section includes emissions from rail and water-borne navigation, but these represent less than 1% of total transportation emissions59.
The biggest share in greenhouse gas emissions related to transportation comes from diesel consumption. Respectively, gasoline, LPG and public transportation electric are the sources that make up the other transportation greenhouse gas inventory (Figure 
22).

The population of İstanbul is forecast (Figure 23) to increase by 22% to 17,9 million in 
2030, by 35% to 19,7 million in 2040 and by 46% to 21,3 million in 2050 compared to 
2015.
In 2040, it is expected that the total number of daily trips will increase to 38,1 million, the total number of daily public transportation trips will increase to 11,1 million, and the share of the rail system in public transportation trips from 24,6% in 2020 to 47,2%. 
In 2020, there are 191 cars per 1.000 people in İstanbul. Considering the current number of registered motor vehicles in the city, it has been determined that if policies to reduce private vehicle use are not implemented, car ownership will increase by 39% between 2020-2040 and traffic congestion problems will continue.
The density of heavy vehicles in the road network causes serious road safety problems as well as carbon emissions and air pollution. In particular, for the problems caused by the circulation of construction materials in the city necessitates the production of safe, environmentally friendly, low-cost and smart logistic solutions.
This means that vehicles fleet also increase together with the other types of public transportation such as railways and buses. It is important for İstanbul to act on this matter considering that it is a coastal city rapid urbanization that is highly vulnerable

Strategic vision is that with integrated and efficient solutions, increasing public transportation for the transportation sector, pedestrianization by increasing the rate of bicycle use, replacement of municipality and service vehicles with low-carbon alternatives, smart signaling and optimization studies, smart parking, etc. It can be said that additional work on shared vehicle use and electric vehicle incentives with applications, the change of public transportation in energy efficient vehicles, and providing a behavioral change in reducing fuel consumption by providing training to drivers who actively use vehicles on economical driving techniques is needed. 
Three categories have been identified as the sources of GHG emissions related with transportation:
-
Transportation on road – municipal vehicle fleet, including affiliate companies;
-
Transportation on railways (trams and subway);
-
Transportation waterborne navigation (public marine transport).
The transportation sector of affiliate companies is responsible for 42,6% of energy consumption of all companies’ consumption. 
So, this is a very important sector and much effort of public institutions and investments to the infrastructure will be needed.
For example, to increase the share of electric vehicles increasement of charging infrastructure is necessary and additional charging should be foreseen in public places, public institutions, companies, buildings and private houses. Together with that the security and reliability of the electricity grid should remain at the same level. İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality

As transport sector consumes 2.184.836,01 MWh of energy, all measures will lead to reduction of energy consumption by 40% or 873.934,4 MWh till 2030. 
During energy consumptions process initial consumption data about energy, was collected from the 28 affiliates/subsidiaries and from this data 7 subsidiaries/affiliate companies were identified as the ones that have the most impact on energy consumptions and who has their energy efficiency plans and targets of energy-using and emission-emitting. These companies are İETT, İSTAÇ, İSTON, İSFALT, İSKİ, İHE and Metro İstanbul (see Section 4). 
In order to reach these targets, the actions they will take measures until 2023 and 2030 as a result of the long-term studies of the 7 subsidiaries/affiliate companies, the reductions they can achieve with their energy efficiency investments and renewable energy investments. 
Apart from these targeted and planned actions, other energy efficiency and renewable energy investments required for 40% reduction by 2030 will be planned and implemented over the years.

5.4.2. Measures for Rapid Transit Railways Under METRO İstanbul
METRO İSTANBUL will reduce energy consumption by 40% in 2019 with its existing and additional energy reduction and renewable energy action plans and investments until 2030 (Table 41). 
The İstanbul Metro is a rapid transit railway network that serves the city of İstanbul, 
Türkiye. It is operated by Metro İstanbul, a public enterprise controlled by the İstanbul 
Metropolitan Municipality. The oldest section of the metro is the M1 line, which opened in 1989; the system now includes 189 stations in service with 929 number of wagons in operation.
The system consists of ten lines: the lines designated M1A, M1B, M2, M3, M6, M7 and 
M9 are on the European side of the Bosphorus, while Lines M4, M5 and M8 are on the 
Asian side. The European and Asian networks do not connect directly but have been linked to each other through the Marmaray system since 2013. İstanbul Metro is connected with the underground systems of the Marmaray tunnel (which connects the lines on the city's European and Asian sides) and the F1 funicular, and with the surface network of the T1 and T4 tram systems as well as the T5 tram.

Optimizing train speeds and modeling expedition planning according to maximum recovery of train braking energy. 
In cases where the expedition planning cannot be modeled, the energy obtained by recycling is pumped back into the grid, converted into a form that can be used in different auxiliary units or used over storage systems. 
The above 2 actions should be applied together in energy saving practices aimed at reducing the use of train energy. It is aimed to improve energy consumption by 40% and 60 million kWh annually on lines where the two actions can be applied together.
At electric vehicle charging stations, in order to reduce AC to DC power losses, an annual improvement of 5 million kWh is aimed by using the DC power supply used by the trains and supporting it with train recovery.

MONITORING OF TRANSPORTATION SECTOR MITIGATION ACTIONS
Establishing a monitoring process is an important part of part of implementation of the SECAP, which allows to measure progress toward the targets set in SECAP.
For each measure, it is very important to determine a measurable and observable indicator that would allow monitoring the progress of the measure and allow timely decisions to be made to ensure the implementation of the measure and the achievement of results. Indicators must be measurable, easily understood and accounted for. It is also necessary to identify responsible persons or institutions for the purposes of monitoring, which will be responsible for the collection and presentation of data. Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 231]
The main results of the energy efficiency studies in the transportation sector presented above for İstanbul are as follows:
1. 
Reduced energy consumption and carbon emissions: 
Improving energy efficiency in transportation would lead to lower energy consumption and carbon emissions, helping to mitigate climate change and improve air quality in İstanbul.
2. 
Lower costs
Energy efficiency measures could also lead to lower fuel and maintenance costs for transport operators and individuals, helping to reduce the overall financial burden of transportation in İstanbul.
3. 
Improved traffic flow
By reducing congestion and travel times, energy-efficient transportation could improve traffic flow and reduce the overall stress and frustration associated with transportation in İstanbul.
4. 
Enhanced quality of life
With less congestion, better air quality, and more efficient transportation options, the quality of life for İstanbul residents could be significantly improved.
5. 
Increased competitiveness
Energy-efficient transportation could also help İstanbul become more competitive, by reducing the overall costs of transportation and making it a more attractive destination for businesses and visitors.
Overall, increasing energy efficiency in the transport sector in İstanbul would have significant economic, social, and environmental benefits, making it a worthwhile investment for the city and its residents.
İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality

[Page 232]
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 234]
6. IMM WASTE, WATER AND 
WASTE WATER ACTION 
AND MITIGATION PLANS

[Page 235]
BACKGROUND 
6.1.1. İstanbul City-Wide Waste Profile
The city-wide waste sector is controlled and managed by IMM through its affiliated company İSTAÇ and district municipalities. 
Mixed domestic wastes collected from households and workplaces by 39 district municipalities are brought to solid waste transfer stations of İstanbul Metropolitan 
Municipality. 
The processes of transportation, recovery, energy generation and final disposal of domestic wastes from solid waste transfer stations to recycling and disposal facilities are managed by İstanbul 
Metropolitan Municipality. An average of 
18.000 tons of household waste is generated daily in İstanbul. As of 2022, 1.162 tons of the waste generated is recycled by the district municipalities, and the remaining 16.838 tons/day of domestic waste is processed by 
IMM by sending 
19% to the 
Waste 
Incineration and Energy Production Facility, 
10% to the recycling facilities and 71% directly to the landfills. 12.015 tons of domestic waste per day is transported by 
IMM to the recycling and disposal facilities from the IMM Solid Waste Transfer Stations on the Anatolian and European Sides with waste transport trucks. Domestic waste production per capita in İstanbul is in the range of 1,1 – 1,2 kg/day.
In accordance with the 
Zero 
Waste 
Regulation and the 
Metropolitan 
Municipality Law, the separate collection and recycling of waste at the source is the responsibility of the district municipalities. By the District Municipalities, packaging wastes and household wastes from households and workplaces are collected separately and the packaging wastes are sent to licensed collection, sorting, and recycling facilities.
Biodegradable waste, such as park and garden waste and marketplace waste are collected separately at the source by the district municipalities and are sent to fermentation in 
Kemerburgaz 
Compost 
Facility. Biodegradable waste is composted and used as a soil conditioner for landscaping purposes in İstanbul's parks and gardens. As of 
2021, food and food waste from institutions and organizations such as hotels and restaurants are collected separately by 
IMM and sent to Biomethanization Facilities, where they are recycled to produce energy and fertilizer.
Industrial quality non-recyclable textiles, paper, bags, nylon, fiber, etc. are collected separately by the district municipalities and are processed in 
Kemerburgaz 
Waste-Derived Fuel Facility to produce solid fuel and are given to cement factories as additional fuel.
An average of 86 tons of medical waste is collected and disposed daily from 9.651 İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality

[Page 236]
institutions, of which 
12% is incinerated in a medical waste incineration facility and remaining 88% is sterilized in the sterilization facility and disposed of in the sanitary landfill.
Landfill gas (methane) generated in landfills is collected by gas collection pipes and burned in gas engines to produce electrical energy. In 2022, IMM produced 1.306.115,5 
MWh of electricity from waste with its recycling and disposal facilities.
 
6.1.2. Waste Water
In İstanbul, İSKİ (İstanbul Water and 
Sewerage 
Administration, affiliated company of IMM) is responsible for water supply and treatment, sewarage system and waste water treatment. Waste water is collected by collectors and directed through tunnels to waste water treatment plants (WWTPs). The total length of the waste water channel network in İstanbul in 2019 was 16.461 km and in 2021 it is 18.304 km. 
According to İSKİ 2019 Activity Report, there are 87 WWTPs in İstanbul with different capacities according to the needs of the areas it serves. In 2022, the number of 
WWTPs increased to 90. Waste water treatment plants are divided according to treatment process types as pre-treatment, biological waste water treatment based on carbon removal, and advanced biological waste water treatment based on nitrogen and phosphorus removal. According to İSKİ 
2019 official data, the total capacity of the listed WWTPs in İstanbul is 5.812.000 m3/day. In 2022, the amount is 6.230.010 m3/day. According to the İSKİ 2019 Annual 
Report, the daily average amount of waste water treated at WWTPs in 2019 is 3.784.358 m3/day. In 2022, the daily average amount of waste water treated at WWTPs was 
4.074.336 m3/day. Many advanced waste water treatment plants have been built taking the sub-basin characteristics into account. Given the two-layer flow structure of the Bosphorus watercourse, the plants were planned as preliminary treatment along the Bosphorus and other plants on the 
Marmara coastal areas have been built with advanced biological treatment specifications. 
Part of the biologically treated effluent is used for the irrigation of recreational areas (parks) as well as for industrial purposes. Significant energy is generated from the treatment plants as well.
 
6.1.3. Potable Water Supply
98% of the water resources of İstanbul are surface water resources. 75% of the water resources are in the Asian part of İstanbul while 25% is within the European part. In contrast, 60% of the population reside in the European section of the city whereas the rest live in the Asian part necessitating transmitting water from Asia to Europe. 
Water from rainfall times is impounded in dams and regulators, and then supplied to 
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 237]
the city following necessary treatment processes. To meet the growing water demand in İstanbul due to population increase and geographical expansion of service areas, potable water is provided from a long range of sub-basins extending from Kırklareli province in Europe to Düzce province in Anatolia. In 2019, İstanbul consumed 1,06 billion m³ water per year and 
2,9 million m3 per day. In 2022, the average water consumption was 
3,02 million m3/day. In the summer season, the city water demand peaks and exceeds 3,5 million m³ per day. The rough terrain of the city and conveying water from far distances lead to high energy consumption for pumping. 
Water is collected in dams and natural lakes, then transferred to treatment plants via transmission lines. There are 18 surface water resources in İstanbul, including 2 natural lakes, 7 dams and 9 regulators. İstanbul has 14 surface water resources with storage, namely 
Pabuçdere, 
Kazandere, 
Sultanbahçe, 
Elmalıdere, 
Büyükdere, Kuzuludere, Düzdere, Terkos, 
Büyükçekmece, 
Sazlıdere, 
Alibeyköy, 
Elmalı-2, Ömerli, and Darlık. However, although the facilities in Sultanbahçedere, 
Elmalıdere, Büyükdere, Kuzuludere and 
Düzdere have storage, these 5 facilities operate like regulators because their active volumes are very limited. In addition, there are 4 facilities, namely Melen, Isaköy, 
Sungurlu and Yesilvadi, where water is taken with a regulator structure that does not have a storage volume. Accordingly, drinking water is provided to İstanbul with 
18 facilities, 9 of which are with storage and 
9 with regulators. Furthermore, there are 
145 potable water wells feeding the regions of Silivri and Çatalca. The annual yield of potable water resources equals 1,6 billion m3. The total amount of raw water taken from water resources in 
2019 was 
1.087.970.256 m3 and 1.075.977,041 m3 of this amount was supplied from surface water resources61.
Water collected in the resources is delivered to drinking water treatment plants and the network via transmission lines reaching a total length of 3.130 km in 2021. The rough geography and distance of water resources to the city brings about a large energy requirement. In every stage between the water resource and house taps, pumping systems are installed to enable pressure supply. In 2021, pumps of various capacities in 119 pumping stations all around İstanbul provide water to all corners of the city. In 
2021, pumps of various capacities in 119 pumping stations located all over İstanbul provide water to all parts of the city. The electrical energy consumption of pumping stations is presented in the İSKİ 
2019 Annual Report. The electrical energy consumption of raw water pumping centers is 690.352.859 kWh/year, the electrical energy consumption of clean water pumping centers is 230.343.454 kWh/year İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality yetraporlari/faaliyetraporu/pdf/2019-FAAL%C4%B0YET-RAPORU.pdf

[Page 238]
and the electrical energy consumption of waste water pumping centers is 18.678.350 kWh/year. Energy supply and efficiency in water sector is analyzed in the Energy 
Efficiency Chapter of IMM SECAP report.
Raw water in the drinking water resources reaches the water treatment plants via transmission lines for the required treatment processes. There are 21 water treatment plants in İstanbul. Ozonation technology is adopted in these facilities with a total capacity of over 4,4 million m3/day in 2019 to enable provision of drinking water complying with national and international standards. The total capacity in 2021 was about 4,9 million m3/day. There are 154 water storage tanks of various sizes in different parts of İstanbul in 2021. 
Constructed to provide water consumption balance, save energy, and minimize water cuts that may occur due to breakdowns and energy cuts, the total capacity of these tanks amounts to 1.792.080 m3 in 2021. 
Upon treatment, the water is supplied to the city via transmission lines and eventually through the drinking water distribution system. The drinking water network was 19.518 km in 2019 and 19.891 km in 2021.
 
6.1.4. Targets and Actions in 
Waste Management 
The "İstanbul Waste 
Management 
Plan" has been prepared in line with the "Deadline 2020" Commitment, which aims to make İstanbul a Carbon 
Neutral and Resistant City by 2050 and will be published after its approval. In the waste management plan, prepared in accordance with the C40 targets and national targets, the goal is to stop dumping the waste directly to the landfills by 2050 and to produce energy from nearly 29% of waste and to recover nearly 71% of the generated waste.
The goal is to build an additional facility with a total capacity of 10.950 tons by the end of 2050, primarily by increasing the investments in the Mechanical 
Biological Treatment Facility. It is also aimed to make an additional investment for waste-to-energy plant, with additional 6.000 tons of waste capacity by the end of 2050. 
IMM has already acted in the waste management sector since C40 report was published and while SECAP report is prepared. 
At the Kemerburgaz Waste Incineration and Energy Generation Facility, which was put into operation in 2021, an average of 3.000 tons of domestic waste is processed per day, and approximately 15-16% of the waste generated in İstanbul is incinerated. 
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 239]
of the domestic waste generated is biodegradable (organic) waste, one of the important topics in reducing and recycling waste is the management of biodegradable wastes. 
In this context, in line with the Provincial 
Environment Board Decision taken in 
2021, biodegradable wastes from places with high biodegradable waste generation throughout İstanbul, such as hotels, restaurants, public institutions and organizations, hospitals, educational institutions, have been started to be collected by IMM. In 
Kemerburgaz 
Biomethanization 
Facility, which was put into operation in 
2021, electrical energy is produced from biogas formed by anaerobic digestion process. 
In the 
Kömürcüoda 
Biomethanization Facility on the Asian side also electrical energy is produced from mixed domestic wastes by anaerobic digestion. 
Biodegradable 
Waste 
Management will be disseminated throughout İstanbul and a large part of the waste will be recovered. In addition, awareness of citizens will be increased by continuing information sharing, trainings and activities within the scope of cooperation with experts on waste management, non-governmental organizations and other civil initiatives.
In the Circular Works Workshop, which was put into operation in 2021, upcycling activities and prototype product designs are carried out with the participation of citizens and producer groups from corporate waste generated from IMM units. The scope, number and effectiveness of Upcycling workshops will be increased. Zero waste certificate has been obtained for 7 main service buildings within the body of 
IMM, and efforts for obtaining zero waste certificates in other buildings and campuses are continuing. At the same time, periodic zero waste awareness training is given in the training module established for all municipal administration employees. 
The operation of the existing facilities, additional investments and other activities are covered by transferring them from the IMM general budget to the 
Waste 
Management 
Branch 
Directorate's budget annually.
 
6.1.5. Targets and Actions in 
Water and Waste Water 
Management
65% of İstanbul`s population live in the 
European part of the city while the rest reside in the Asian part. Yet, the case is the opposite when it comes to water resources. 
For this very reason, transferring water between the continents was inevitable. 
Considering the population expected to top 
20 million in the future, the Greater İstanbul 
Water Supply project has been undertaken İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality

[Page 240]
by the State Hydraulic Works (DSİ) under the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry to supply the city’s ever-growing water needs. 
In an inter-basin and inter-continental manner, water is taken from the Melen 
Creek in another province, Düzce, from 170 km and Bosphorus Crossing Tunnel was established. 
Besides the tunnel section, the Greater İstanbul Water Supply Melen System62 project to secure the drinking water supply to İstanbul until the year 2071, includes the 
Cumhuriyet 
Water 
Treatment 
Plant (capacity of 720.000 m3/day), the Melen 
Transmission Line and pumping stations, the 
Melen 
Dam (total impoundment volume of 694 million m3) and Regulator and the Sungurlu Dam. The completed facilities (Cumhuriyet Water Treatment 
Plant, 
Melen 
Transmission 
Line and 
Bosphorus Tunnel) have been transferred to İSKİ for operation and maintenance.
İSKİ is actively executing different actions to improve waste water management capacity. 
Waste water construction activities carried out by İSKİ include all kinds of waste water networks, collectors, pumping stations and lines and tunnel constructions, creek rehabilitation and storm water canal constructions with its jurisdiction.

6.4. SUMMARY İstanbul 
Metropolitan 
Municipality through its affiliated company İSTAÇ and district municipalities are responsible of waste management sector in İstanbul city. Approximately 
18.000 tons of municipal waste is collected each day in İstanbul and domestic waste production per capita is in range of 1,1-1,2 kg/day. According to 
Zero 
Waste 
Regulation and the 
Metropolitan Municipality Law, the waste is collected separately by type at the source and recycling is responsibility of the district municipalities. Today biodegradable waste is collected and composted in Kemerburgaz Compost 
Facility and used as a soil conditioner for green areas in Instanbul. Also, from 
2021 food waste from different institutions are collected and treated in biomethanization facilites and energy and fertilizers are produced. Industrial quality non-recyvlable materials are collected and processed in 
Kemerburgaz 
Waste-Derived 
Fuel 
Facility and RDF (refuse-derivied fuel) is produced. Medical waste is either incinerated in special incineration facility or sterilized and disposed to landfill. Landfill gas is collected from landfilles to produce electricity. 
The "İstanbul Waste 
Management 
Plan" has been prepared in line with the "Deadline 2020" Commitment, which aims to make İstanbul a Carbon 
Neutral and Resistant City by 2050 and will be published after its approval. In the waste management plan, prepared in accordance with the C40 targets and national targets, the goal is to stop disposing the waste directly to the landfills by 2050 and to produce energy from ca 29% of waste and to recover ca 
71% of the generated waste. IMM has made strategic plans and already taken actions to improve collection process of different waste type and increase the capacity to recycle, reuse and energy production from waste and also to rise awareness among citizens and instititions to avoid of producing of waste. İSKİ is responsible for water supply and treatment, sewarage system and waste water treatment in İstanbul. 
According to İSKİ 2019 Activity Report, there were 87 WWTPs in İstanbul with different capacities according to the needs of the areas it serves (in 2022 are 
90 WWTPs) and the daily average amount of waste water treated at 
WWTPs in 2019 was 3.784.358 m3/day (in 2022, 4.074.336 m3/day). İSKİ is actively executing different actions to improve waste water management capacity and find possibilities for waste water recovery and reuse. İstanbul Metropolitan Municipality

[Page 252]
98% of the water resources of İstanbul are surface water resources. To meet the growing water demand in İstanbul due to population increase and geographical expansion of service areas, potable water is provided from a long range of sub-basins extending from Kırklareli province in Europe to 
Düzce province in Anatolia. In 2019, İstanbul consumed 1,06 billion m³ water per year and 2,9 million m3 per day (in 
2022, 3,02 million m3/day). The rough terrain of the city and conveying water from far distances lead to high energy consumption for pumping. Thus, it is essential to find different solutions (technical and awareness rising) to reduce water consumption and water losses. 
The waste and waste water treatment capacity for baseline year 2019 was mapped to calculate GHG emissions. 
Baseline inventory shows that IMM corporate waste and waste water treatment emissions (42.459 MtCO2e) comprise about 3% of total municipal corporate emissions. Main source of corporate emissions is solid waste disposal and incineration. The majority of emissions from the waste sector, detailed in this report, originate from the solid waste disposal and incineration sub-sectors. İstanbul is committed to reducing its 
GHG emissions in the future and the goal is to achieve net-zero emissions by 
2050. Thus IMM has set effective targets for emission reduction in waste, water and waste water sector. IMM target in waste sector is to improve waste management practices and increase waste recovery rates by 2050. 
It is essential to decrease the rate of water losses and water usage in water sector and to improve waste water recovery and reuse in waste water sector. 
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 254]
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 256]
BUSINESS 
AS 
USUAL (BAU) 
SCENARIO (IMM)
According to strategic documents 
IMM’s goal is to achieve net-zero emissions by 2050. BEI has shown that total IMM emissions in 2019 were 
1.544.908 ktCO2e, and if anything less would be done, this would only increase.
The business as usual (BAU) scenario assumes the changes to the GHG emissions in the BEI sectors over the period 
2019-2030 without climate change mitigation actions within IMM which have been considered in this document but including national-level measures. The changes are driven by the changes in socio-economic parameters (such as population and 
GDP) and the introduction of nationwide measures that are outside of the municipality’s influence. 
Energy consumption and 
GHG emissions in IMM’s stationary energy sector are projected to decrease gradually due to national energy efficiency legal measures in public and commercial buildings, municipal public street lighting, application of more efficient space heating solutions. IMM transport sector is planned to grow due to national strategic goals to increase the share of railroads and urban public transport. Therefore, an annual increase in final fuel and electricity consumption in the transport sector is foreseen. GHG emissions from the waste sector in the municipality are predicted to increase. 
According to the BAU scenario, with the continued growth of the city’s population and economy, the emissions at IMM level in 2030 are expected to grow by 5,0% compared to 2019 with emissions in transport sector growing by 24,3%, energy use and subsequent 
GHG emissions in the stationary energy sector decreasing by 
10,5% and emissions in waste sector rising by 11%. 
Total reported GHG emissions of IMM would be over 1.620.560 tCO2e per year in 2030 (Figure 24).
Sustainable Energy and Climate Action Plan of İstanbul

[Page 257]
MITIGATION SCENARIO
The climate change mitigation scenario assumes the implementation of mitigation actions described in this document (see 
Buildings and Transport Chapters). The total sum of predicted GHG reductions in 
Stationary energy (Buildings) and Transport sectors was calculated encompassing measures of IMM affiliates and subsidiary companies aimed at reducing energy and fuel consumption till 2030 by 40%. 
GHG emission reduction targets of the measures described in previous chapters are expressed in anticipated energy and fuel savings converted to energy savings per year (MWh/yr) in Stationary energy and 
Transport sectors. These energy savings were converted to GHG emission savings assuming that proportions of fuel and energy use in final energy consumption will remain the same as in 2019 and multiplying the shares by respective emission factors.
The implementation of these actions results in a projected total emission reduction of 
40% compared to the BEI and 42,8% compared to BAU scenario (Table 51). 
Reduction of CO2e emissions in 2030 will mostly be the result of improvements in energy efficiency in municipal and commercial buildings, urban planning and the positive changes in public transport sector (increase of railroad share thus reducing the number of diesel-driven buses, implementing sustainable mobility actions, etc.).

It should be noted that Stationary energy and Transport sectors of IMM have potential to achieve even higher GHG emission reductions and have demonstrated ambition to reach the zero-emission state in 2050. For this reason, it is highly likely that IMM's corporate greenhouse gas emissions will have decreased by more than 
40% by 2030. As IMM’s areas of activity are closely related to the İstanbul city’s main activity sectors, the achievement of the longer period targets will strongly depend on the collaboration between the municipality’s institutions, industry, commercial and other sectors.

According to GCoM requirements, the city should regularly monitor progress in implementing the action plan and toward achieving the targets and goals set. 
Monitoring of SECAP implementation is conducted by each individual city and local government in accordance with locally applicable rules and provisions as identified in the plan. The monitoring information can be reported through the recognized online reporting platforms:
Table 52 provides an overview of the most important elements a city-level monitoring framework related to the climate action plan(s) put in place under the GCoM should contain and explains the frequency and elements of reporting to the GCoM.
CDP-ICLEI unified reporting system the SECAP reporting platform, available in “MyCovenant” (the European Covenant

Monitoring Element
Reporting to GCoM
GHG Emissions Inventory 
Regular update of the GHG emissions inventory. The city is required to keep track of the city-wide emissions. 
When updating inventories, cities must take into consideration all possible changes outlined in Table 6 in chapter 3, even if those changes are not significant. 
Every two years 
A more recent inventory must be reported to GCoM.

Inventory update due to significant changes 
Signatories are required to update their inventories in case significant changes take place that trigger a recalculation of the inventory (incl. changes in inventory boundary, calculation methodology, improvements in data accuracy, discovery of errors, etc.). This may also trigger the need for a recalculation of historic inventories (see chapter 3 for further details).
